## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the core ODE formulation in population dynamics. The relationship captures how biological populations change due to reproduction, competition, and environmental factors.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * P / (P + c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (per-capita growth increasing then decreasing)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent growth minus removal)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with saturation minus mortality)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing exponentially with time)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic with periodic forcing)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoidal growth model)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order competition terms)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism scaling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Cubic terms in P (c0*P - c1*P^2 + c2*P^3 or similar) → Allee effect or bistability in population dynamics
- dP/dt proportional to P*(1 - f(P)) → density-dependent regulation where f(P) captures intraspecific competition
- Negative quadratic term -c*P^2 alongside positive linear term c*P → carrying capacity limitation from resource competition
- Logarithmic dependence log(P) in growth rate → Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate declines logarithmically
- Ratio P/(P+c) in growth expression → type II functional response or mate-finding limitation at low density
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) modulating growth → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing
- Fractional power P^c with 0<c<1 → surface-area-to-volume scaling in metabolic growth models
- Product of two linear factors in P → two critical population values (extinction threshold and carrying capacity)

I need to determine if any candidate formula can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT: `c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*P*exp(-c3*t)`**

which equals `0.2569*P*sin(0.7218*t) + 0.1149*P*exp(-0.03038*t)`

This has the structure: `P * [A*sin(B*t) + C*exp(D*t)]` where A, B, C, D are specific constants.

Key observations about GT:
- It's linear in P (every term has exactly P^1)
- It has a sin term and an exp term, both multiplied by P
- No constant offset (no terms independent of P)
- sin(c1*t) = cos(c1*t - π/2), so sin and cos forms are interchangeable with phase shift

= P*[c0*sin(c2*t + c1) + c3*exp(c4*t)]

**Candidate 15: `P*c0*cos(c1*t + c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t)`**
cos(c1*t + c2) = sin(c1*t + c2 + π/2). Setting c2 = -π/2, c1=0.7218, c0=0.2569, c3=0.1149, c4=-0.03038. This matches GT. ✓

Setting c0=0, this reduces to candidate 15's form. ✓

**Candidate 29: `P*c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5`**
Setting c5=0, this reduces to candidate 14's form. ✓

**Candidate 42: `P*c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P**c5*c6`**

Setting c6=0, c7=0, reduces to candidate 14. ✓

**GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*P*exp(-c3*t)**

This is: P*(A*sin(B*t) + C*exp(-D*t)) where A, B, C, D are fixed positive constants.

Key structural features:
- Linear in P (every term is proportional to P)
- Has a P*sin(ωt) term (note: sin, not cos, and no phase shift - starts at 0)
- Has a P*exp(-αt) term (exponential decay)
- No constant offset terms
- No terms involving log, P², P³, P/(P+c), etc.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** Complex rational expression with P/(P+c3) structure plus log term. Cannot reduce to pure P*f(t).
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Factor: P²(c0*sin+c4*exp) + P(c6*sin'+c8*exp) all over (P+c3). For this to equal P*(A*sin+B*exp), need [P²(c0*sin+c4*exp)+P(c6*sin'+c8*exp)]/(P+c3) = P*(A*sin+B*exp). So P(c0*sin+c4*exp)+c6*sin'+c8*exp = (P+c3)*(A*sin+B*exp). Expanding: P*A*sin+P*B*exp+c3*A*sin+c3*B*exp. Matching: c0=A, c4=B, c6*sin(c1*t+c7)=c3*A*sin(c1*t+c2), c8=c3*B. So c7=c2, c6=c3*A, c8=c3*B. This works! ✓
